Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the discharge to 2.5 V, the V 2p<sub>3/2</sub> peak returned to its original position, indicating the reduction of V<sup>4+</sup> to V<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0040_R_d19537802e1821" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nano Energy">40</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0043_R_d19537802e1821" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The ex situ XPS spectrum of V2p for the NKCMVP (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10a</a>, Supporting Information) exhibits the identical valence changes with the NKCMVP-Zr0.2. Generally, the degree of splitting (∆E) of the Mn3s peaks can show more precise indication of the oxidation state of Mn.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0007_R_d19537802e1829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0020_R_d19537802e1829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To analyze the change in the Mn valence state more accurately in the NKCMVP-Zr0.2, the ex situ XPS spectra of Mn 3s and Mn 2p were investigated. The ex situ XPS spectra of Mn 2p (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0006">6e</a>) reveal that upon charging to 3.6 V, the characteristic peak of Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub> located at ≈641.9 eV, shifts to a higher binding energy of ≈642.2 eV, indicating the oxidation of Mn<sup>2+</sup> to Mn<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0007_R_d19537802e1844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0015_R_d19537802e1844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Inorg. Chem. Front.">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0020_R_d19537802e1844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0040_R_d19537802e1844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nano Energy">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Upon discharge to 2.5V, the characteristic peak of Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub> returns to ≈641.9 eV, suggesting that Mn<sup>3+</sup> was re-reduced to Mn<sup>2+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0040_R_d19537802e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nano Energy">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The spectra of Mn 3s (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0006">6d</a>) at the corresponding potential further confirm this phenomenon. At voltages below 3.6 V, the ∆E is ≈6.0 eV, indicating that the Mn ion exists in the form of +2 valence.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0006_R_d19537802e1865" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Energy Mater.">6</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0020_R_d19537802e1865" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> With an increase in charging voltage, the ∆E gradually reduces to ≈5.4 eV, confirming the phenomenon that Mn<sup>2+</sup> was gradually oxidized to Mn<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0007_R_d19537802e1874" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Upon discharge to 2.5 V, the ∆E increases back to ≈6.0 eV, further confirming the reduction of Mn<sup>3+</sup> to Mn<sup>2+</sup>, which is consistent with the changes in Mn valence observed in the NKCMVP (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10b,c</a>, Supporting Information). The ex situ XPS spectra of Zr (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0006">6f</a>) reveal that during charging-discharging process, the characteristic peaks of Zr 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and Zr 3d<sub>3/2</sub> were consistently located at ≈183.2 eV and ≈185.6 eV within the voltage range of 2.5–3.8 V, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0029_R_d19537802e1895" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Storage Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This indicates that Zr ion did not participate in electrochemical reactions.</p>
         
         <p>It is well known that the NMVP cathode material undergoes the oxidation reaction from V<sup>3+</sup>→V<sup>4+</sup> to Mn<sup>2+</sup>→Mn<sup>3+</sup> sequentially during the sodium extraction process in the voltage range of 2.5–3.8 V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0044_R_d19537802e1911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">44</a>-<a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0046_R_d19537802e1911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Chem. Mater.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To deepen and verify the effect of Zr<sup>4+</sup> on the structural and electrochemical properties of the materials. The density of states (DOS) for both pristine Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/Na<sub>3.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and de-sodiated Na<sub>2</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/Na<sub>1.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> materials were calculated to investigate the impact of Zr substitution on electronic conductivity. Additionally, to better elucidate the Zr-substitution effect, K<sup>+</sup> and Ca<sup>2+</sup> ions were neglected in the calculation process. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0007">7a,b</a> depict the structural models of Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, along with their respective DOS. The spin-up part of Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> has a band gap of 1.103 eV, showing typical semi-metallic properties. The spin-up part of the Na<sub>3.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> has no band gap and shows metallic properties. This suggests that the substitution of Zr<sup>4+</sup> enhances the metallic abundance of the material, which may be attributed to the introduction of the 4d Zr element to increase the number of electrons in the material system, thereby improving electronic conductivity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0020_R_d19537802e2001" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0047_R_d19537802e2001" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - J. Power Sources">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0007">7c,d</a> shows the structural models of Na<sub>2</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>1.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and their corresponding DOS. With the extraction of sodium ions from the materials, the materials all show metallic properties, indicating the enhancement of electronic conductivity during the extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> from the framework. And the V and Mn orbitals located in the valence band appear in the conduction band, respectively, indicating that the successive oxidation reactions are associated with the electron loss of V and Mn.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0033_R_d19537802e2029" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Nano">33</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0048_R_d19537802e2029" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - J. Mater. Chem. A">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The narrowing of the spin-down band gap with the Na<sup>+</sup> ions extraction is primarily attributed to the proximity of the O 2p orbitals located in the valence band to the Fermi energy level, and some literature has suggested that O acts as a charge-transfer mediator between the TM cations (Mn<sup>2+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>) and Na<sup>+</sup> ions during the charging and discharging process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0046_R_d19537802e2043" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Chem. Mater.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Mn elements in the de-sodiated Na<sub>2</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>1.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> structures are in the high-spin Mn<sup>3+</sup> oxidation state, which may lead to JT distortions of the MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedra in the materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0012_R_d19537802e2070" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Small">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0021_R_d19537802e2070" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Energy Lett.">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202418642-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202418642-bib-0033_R_d19537802e2070" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Nano">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The JT distortions are mainly due to the contraction or elongation of Mn─O bonds along the axial direction of the Mn─O bonding in the octahedral units. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0007">7e,f</a> shows the structural model diagrams of MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedra in the Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/de-sodiated Na<sub>2</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/de-sodiated Na<sub>1.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> structures, respectively. Analysis of the changes in MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedral bond lengths during charging and discharging process reveals that the introduction of Zr<sup>4+</sup> can mitigate the deformation of the MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedral structure. This finding further confirms that Zr substitution promotes the reduction of Mn ion dissolution and enhances the structural stability of the material. In addition, the diffusion paths and diffusion energy barriers of Na<sup>+</sup> ions were investigated using the CI-NEB (climbing-image nudged elastic band) method. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0007">7g</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information) depict the migration path diagrams of Na<sup>+</sup> from Na(2) to the Na(1) site, along with their corresponding migration energy barriers for Na<sub>3.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, respectively. Migration energy barriers for Na<sub>4</sub>MnV(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3.6</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>VZr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> are 0.358 and 0.222 eV, respectively, suggesting that Zr<sup>4+</sup> can efficiently lower migration energy barriers of sodium ions and boost Na<sup>+</sup> migration. These calculated results align with experimental findings, confirming that Zr<sup>4+</sup> doping promotes enhancements in electronic conductivity and ion diffusion rate, thereby leading to superior electrochemical properties of the material.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202418642-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7493d656-a207-4c94-9e6b-15a4167ed7e2/adfm202418642-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7493d656-a207-4c94-9e6b-15a4167ed7e2/adfm202418642-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b233b489-fa8f-43d9-8d19-5300956a4c8b/adfm202418642-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7493d656-a207-4c94-9e6b-15a4167ed7e2/adfm202418642-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202418642-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202418642" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The structural models and DOS of Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; b)the structural models and DOS of Na<sub>3.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; c) the structural models and DOS of Na<sub>2</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; d) the structural models and DOS of Na<sub>1.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; e) the structural model diagrams of MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedra in the Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/desodiated Na<sub>2</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; f) the structural model diagrams of MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedra in the Na<sub>3.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/desodiated Na<sub>1.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>; g) migration path diagrams of Na<sup>+</sup> from Na(2) to the Na(1) site of Na<sub>3.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, and migration energy barriers for Na<sub>3.6</sub>VMn<sub>0.8</sub>Zr<sub>0.2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>4</sub>VMn(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To evaluate the practicality of the developed NKCMVP-Zr0.2, full cell was assembled using NKCMVP-Zr0.2 as cathode and hard carbon (HC) as anode (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0008">8a</a>). The reversible discharge specific capacity of HC at 0.1 C (1 C = 250 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) was ≈315 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> in the voltage window of 0.01-3.0 V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0008">8b</a>). The assembled NKCMVP-Zr0.2//HC full cell was evaluated at an operating voltage window of 2.5–3.8 V. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0008">8c</a>, the charge and discharge profiles of the full cell display one voltage plateau at 3.45 V with discharge specific capacity of ≈83 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 C, In addition, the rate performance and cycling performance of the full cells were tested as well. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12a</a> (Supporting Information), the discharge specific capacities at 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 C are 75.8, 69.5, 64.0, and 54.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, and their corresponding rate capability curves are depicted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12b</a> (Supporting Information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202418642-fig-0008">8d</a> exhibits a discharge capacity of 66.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 1 C with a capacity retention of 84.3%, demonstrating superior sodium storage capability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202418642-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4a9c7faa-2e62-422b-a7f0-509ffde21474/adfm202418642-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4a9c7faa-2e62-422b-a7f0-509ffde21474/adfm202418642-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/dbd27c79-7e7f-43ea-a128-9bbf708b04f3/adfm202418642-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4a9c7faa-2e62-422b-a7f0-509ffde21474/adfm202418642-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202418642-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202418642" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of the NKCMVP-Zr0.2 cathode // HC anode sodium ion full battery; b) the charge–discharge curves of the NKCMVP-Zr0.2 cathode and HC anode; c) the charge–discharge curves of the NKCMVP-Zr0.2 cathode // HC anode full cell at 0.1C; d) cycling performance of the full cell at 1 C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202418642-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202418642-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, one-step de-sodiation of the NMVP cathode for SIBs has been successfully achieved via regulating the coordination environment of Mn sites using Zr<sup>4+</sup> substitution. Based on DFT theoretical calculation, ex situ XRD, and electrochemical evaluation (GITT, charge, and discharge tests, etc), the introduction of Zr<sup>4+</sup> can efficiently reduce Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier and significantly improve Na<sup>+</sup> migration capability in the second step Na<sup>+</sup> de-sodiation reaction (the rate-determining step of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion), realize one-step completion of the whole Na<sup>+</sup> extraction processes of NMVP cathode, which involves usually a typical two-step reaction with an order of magnitude difference in Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient. Moreover, the Na-site modulation by K<sup>+</sup> and Ca<sup>2+</sup> can also alter the local coordination environment of Na-O and boost Na<sup>+</sup> migration. Besides the improvement of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, Zr<sup>4+</sup> modulation at Mn sites can also inhibit the JT distortion of Mn and obviously enhance the structural stability for enduring repeated Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction, leading to excellent cycling life. When evaluated as cathode for SIBs, the obtained NKCMVP-Zr0.2 exhibits the most optimized sodium storage performance with a specific capacity of 73 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 15 C, a capacity retention of 92.7% at 10 C after 3000 cycles at room temperature, and a capacity retention of 72.6% at 1 C after 1000 cycles at 50&nbsp;°C. Our findings open the possibility of designing and optimizing intercalation-based cathode materials with a one-step de-sodiation reaction via regulating the coordination environment of TM sites. This work also offers guidance for designing advanced cathode materials for rechargeable batteries with high-rate capability and long cycle life.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
